   <h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">
    Help:IPA
   </h1>
   <div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
    <div id="siteSub">
     From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia
    </div>
    <div id="contentSub">
     <span class="mw-redirectedfrom">
      (Redirected from
      <a href="/w/index.php?title=Wikipedia:IPA&amp;redirect=no" title="Wikipedia:IPA">
       Wikipedia:IPA
      </a>
      )
     </span>
    </div>
    <div class="mw-jump" id="jump-to-nav">
     Jump to:
     <a href="#mw-head">
      navigation
     </a>
     ,
     <a href="#p-search">
      search
     </a>
    </div>
    <div class="mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en">
     <div class="hatnote">
      For help installing IPA-compatible fonts, see
      <a href="/wiki/Help:Special_characters#IPA_symbols" title="Help:Special characters">
       Help:Special characters IPA symbols
      </a>
      .
     </div>
     <div class="hatnote">
      For a basic introduction to using IPA written for English readers, see
      <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Introduction" title="Help:IPA/Introduction">
       Help:IPA/Introduction
      </a>
      .
     </div>
     <table class="metadata mbox-small selfref noprint" style="border:1px solid #aaa;background-color:#f9f9f9;width:22em;">
      <tr>
       <td class="mbox-image">
        <img alt="" data-file-height="128" data-file-width="128" height="40" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Gnome-speakernotes.svg/40px-Gnome-speakernotes.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Gnome-speakernotes.svg/60px-Gnome-speakernotes.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Gnome-speakernotes.svg/80px-Gnome-speakernotes.svg.png 2x" width="40"/>
       </td>
       <td class="mbox-text plainlist" style="font-size:95%;">
        <b>
         This article includes inline links to audio files.
        </b>
        If you have trouble playing the files, see
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Media_help" title="Wikipedia:Media help">
         Wikipedia Media help
        </a>
        .
       </td>
      </tr>
     </table>
     <p>
      Here is a basic
      <b>
       key
      </b>
      to the symbols of the
      <b>
       <a href="/wiki/International_Phonetic_Alphabet" title="International Phonetic Alphabet">
        International Phonetic Alphabet
       </a>
      </b>
      . For the smaller set of symbols that is sufficient for English, see
      <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English" title="Help:IPA for English">
       Help:IPA for English
      </a>
      . Several rare IPA symbols are not included; these are found in the
      <a href="/wiki/International_Phonetic_Alphabet" title="International Phonetic Alphabet">
       main IPA article
      </a>
      . For the Manual of Style guideline for pronunciation, see
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style_(pronunciation)" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style (pronunciation)">
       Wikipedia:Manual of Style (pronunciation)
      </a>
      .
      <span id="top">
      </span>
     </p>
     <p>
      For each IPA symbol, an English example is given where possible; here "RP" stands for
      <a href="/wiki/Received_Pronunciation" title="Received Pronunciation">
       Received Pronunciation
      </a>
      . The foreign languages that are used to illustrate additional sounds are primarily the ones most likely to be familiar to English speakers,
      <a href="/wiki/French_phonology" title="French phonology">
       French
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/German_phonology" title="German phonology">
       German
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/Spanish_phonology" title="Spanish phonology">
       Spanish
      </a>
      . For symbols not covered by those, recourse is taken to the populous languages
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Standard_Mandarin#Phonology" title="Standard Mandarin">
       Mandarin Chinese
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hindi-Urdu_phonology" title="Hindi-Urdu phonology">
       Hindustani
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Arabic_phonology" title="Arabic phonology">
       Arabic
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/Russian_phonology" title="Russian phonology">
       Russian
      </a>
      . For sounds still not covered, other smaller but well-known languages are used, such as
      <a href="/wiki/Swahili_language#Sounds" title="Swahili language">
       Swahili
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Turkish_phonology" title="Turkish phonology">
       Turkish
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/Zulu_language#phonology" title="Zulu language">
       Zulu
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      The left-hand column displays the symbols like this:
      <a href="/wiki/File:Open_front_unrounded_vowel.ogg" title="File:Open front unrounded vowel.ogg">
       <sup>
        (i)
       </sup>
      </a>
      <span class="audiolink">
       <a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/65/Open_front_unrounded_vowel.ogg" title="listen">
        <img alt="listen" data-file-height="11" data-file-width="11" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Speakerlink-new.svg/11px-Speakerlink-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Speakerlink-new.svg/17px-Speakerlink-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Speakerlink-new.svg/22px-Speakerlink-new.svg.png 2x" width="11"/>
       </a>
      </span>
      <span class="IPA">
       <a href="/wiki/Open_front_unrounded_vowel" title="Open front unrounded vowel">
        <big>
         [a]
        </big>
       </a>
      </span>
      . Click on the speaker icon to hear the sound; click on the symbol itself for a dedicated article with a more complete description and examples from multiple languages. All the sounds are spoken more than once, and the consonant sounds are spoken once followed by a vowel and once between vowels.
     </p>

     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Main_symbols">
       Main symbols
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      The symbols are arranged by similarity to letters of the Latin alphabet. Symbols which do not resemble any Latin letter are placed at the end.
     </p>

     <ul>
      <li>
       <span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_d">
        <b>
         <a href="#ref_d">
          ^1
         </a>
        </b>
       </span>
       <span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_t">
        <b>
         <a href="#ref_t">
          ^2
         </a>
        </b>
       </span>
       These symbols are officially written with a tie linking them (
       <i>
        e.g.
       </i>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        t
       </span>
       ), and are also sometimes written as single characters (
       <i>
        e.g.
       </i>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        
       </span>
       ) though the latter convention is no longer official. They are written without ligatures here to ensure correct display in all browsers.
      </li>
     </ul>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Diacritic_marks">
       Diacritic marks
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      All
      <a href="/wiki/Diacritic" title="Diacritic">
       diacritics
      </a>
      are here shown on a carrier letter such as the vowel
      <i>
       a.
      </i>
     </p>
     <table class="wikitable" style="margin: 1em">
      <tr>
       <th>
        Symbol
       </th>
       <th>
        Example
       </th>
       <th colspan="2">
        Description
       </th>
      </tr>
      <tr>
       <td align="center">
        <a href="/wiki/Stress_(linguistics)" title="Stress (linguistics)">
         <big>
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           [ a ]
          </span>
         </big>
        </a>
       </td>
       <td rowspan="2">
        <i>
         pronunciation
        </i>
        <br/>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         [pnnsien]
        </span>
       </td>
       <td colspan="2">
        Main stress. The mark denotes the stress of the
        <i>
         following
        </i>
        syllable.
       </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
       <td align="center">
        <a href="/wiki/Secondary_stress" title="Secondary stress">
         <big>
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           [ a ]
          </span>
         </big>
        </a>
       </td>
       <td colspan="2">
        Weaker stress. The mark denotes the stress of the
        <i>
         following
        </i>
        syllable.
       </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
       <td align="center">
        <a href="/wiki/Length_(phonetics)" title="Length (phonetics)">

           [ a ]
          </span>
         </big>
        </a>

         []
        </span>
       </td>

        <i>
         Mayo
        </i>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /meo/
        </span>
        for
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">

        </span>
        ,

        </i>

     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Brackets">
       Brackets
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      Two types of brackets are commonly used to enclose transcriptions in the IPA:
     </p>
     <ul>
      <li>
       /Slashes/ indicate those meaningful sounds that are distinguished as the basic sounds of a language by native speakers; these are called
       <a href="/wiki/Phoneme" title="Phoneme">
        phonemes
       </a>
       . Changing the symbols between slashes would either change the identity of the word or produce nonsense. For example, since there is no meaningful difference to a native speaker between the two sounds written with the letter el in the word
       <i>
        lulls,
       </i>
       they are considered the same phoneme and so, using slashes, they are given the same symbol in IPA:
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /llz/
       </span>
       . Similarly, Spanish
       <i>
        la bomba
       </i>
       is transcribed phonemically with two instances of the same
       <i>
        b
       </i>
       sound,
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /labomba/
       </span>
       , despite the fact that they sound different to a speaker of English. Thus a reader who is not familiar with the language in question might not know how to interpret these transcriptions more narrowly.
      </li>
      <li>
       [Square brackets] indicate the narrower or more detailed
       <a href="/wiki/Phonetics" title="Phonetics">
        phonetic
       </a>
       qualities of a pronunciation, not taking into account the norms of the language to which it belongs; therefore, such transcriptions do not regard whether subtly different sounds in the pronunciation are actually noticeable or distinguishable to a native speaker of the language. Within square brackets is what a foreigner who does not know the structure of a language might hear as discrete units of sound. For instance, the English word
       <i>
        lulls
       </i>
       may be pronounced in a particular dialect more specifically as
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [lz]
       </span>
       , with different letter el sounds at the beginning and end. This may be obvious to speakers of other languages that differentiate between the sounds
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [l]
       </span>
       and
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        []
       </span>
       . Likewise, Spanish
       <i>
        la bomba
       </i>
       (pronounced without a pause) has two different b-sounds to the ears of foreigners or linguists
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [laomba]
       </span>
       though a native Spanish speaker might not be able to hear it. Omitting or adding such detail does not make a difference to the identity of the word, but helps to give a more precise pronunciation.
      </li>
     </ul>
     <p>
      A third kind of bracket is occasionally seen:
     </p>
     <ul>
      <li>
       Either //double slashes// or |pipes| (or occasionally other conventions) show that the enclosed sounds are theoretical constructs that are not actually heard. (This is part of
       <a href="/wiki/Morphophonology" title="Morphophonology">
        morphophonology
       </a>
       .) For instance, most phonologists argue that the
       <i>
        -s
       </i>
       at the ends of verbs, which surfaces as either
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /s/
       </span>
       in
       <i>
        talks
       </i>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /tks/
       </span>
       or as
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /z/
       </span>
       in
       <i>
        lulls
       </i>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /llz/
       </span>
       , has a single underlying form. If they decide this form is an
       <i>
        s,
       </i>
       they would write it //s// (or |s|) to claim that phonemic
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /tks/
       </span>
       and
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /llz/
       </span>
       are essentially
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        //tks//
       </span>
       and
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        //lls//
       </span>
       underneath. If they were to decide it was essentially the latter, //z//, they would transcribe these words
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        //tkz//
       </span>
       and
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        //llz//
       </span>
       .
      </li>
     </ul>
     <p>
      Lastly,
     </p>
     <ul>
      <li>
       <span class="Unicode">
        
       </span>
       Angle brackets
       <span class="Unicode">
        
       </span>
       are used to set off
       <a href="/wiki/Orthography" title="Orthography">
        orthography
       </a>
       , as well as
       <a href="/wiki/Transliteration" title="Transliteration">
        transliteration
       </a>
       from non-Latin scripts. Thus
       <span class="Unicode">
        
       </span>
       lulls
       <span class="Unicode">
        
       </span>
       ,
       <span class="Unicode">
        
       </span>
       la bomba
       <span class="Unicode">
        
       </span>
       , the letter
       <span class="Unicode">
        
       </span>
       a
       <span class="Unicode">
        
       </span>
       . Angle brackets are not supported by all fonts, so a template {{
       <a href="/wiki/Template:Angle_bracket" title="Template:Angle bracket">
        angle bracket
       </a>
       }} (shortcut {{
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Template:Angbr" title="Template:Angbr">
        angbr
       </a>
       }}) is used to ensure maximal compatibility. (Comment there if you're having problems.)
      </li>
     </ul>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Rendering_issues">
       Rendering issues
      </span>

     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Voiced_velar_plosive">
       Voiced velar plosive
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      These two characters should look similar:
     </p>
     <dl>
      <dd>
       <table class="wikitable">
        <tr>
         <td>
          <big>
           <big>
            <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
             
            </span>
           </big>
          </big>
         </td>
         <td>
          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Opentail_g.svg">
           <img alt="Opentail g.svg" data-file-height="196" data-file-width="115" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Opentail_g.svg/8px-Opentail_g.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Opentail_g.svg/12px-Opentail_g.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Opentail_g.svg/16px-Opentail_g.svg.png 2x" width="8"/>
          </a>
         </td>
        </tr>
       </table>
      </dd>
     </dl>
     <p>
      If in the box to the left you see the symbol
      <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%C9%A1MSReferenceSansSerif.png">
       <img alt="MSReferenceSansSerif.png" data-file-height="69" data-file-width="59" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/%C9%A1MSReferenceSansSerif.png/12px-%C9%A1MSReferenceSansSerif.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/%C9%A1MSReferenceSansSerif.png/18px-%C9%A1MSReferenceSansSerif.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/%C9%A1MSReferenceSansSerif.png/24px-%C9%A1MSReferenceSansSerif.png 2x" width="12"/>
      </a>
      rather than a lower-case open-tail g, you may be experiencing a well-known bug in the font
      <i>
       MS Reference Sans Serif
      </i>
      ; switching to another font may fix it.
     </p>

     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Affricates_and_double_articulation">
       Affricates and double articulation
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      The
      <i>
       tie bar
      </i>
      is intended to cover both letters of an affricate or doubly articulated consonant. However, if your browser uses Arial Unicode MS to display IPA characters, the following incorrectly formed sequences may look better than the correct order (letter, tie bar, letter) because of a bug in that font:
     </p>
     <dl>
      <dd>
       ts, t, t, dz, d, d, t, kp, b, m.
      </dd>
     </dl>
     <p>
      Here is how the proper configuration displays in your default IPA font:
     </p>
     <dl>
      <dd>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        ts, dz, t, d, t, d, t, kp, b, m
       </span>
       ,
      </dd>
     </dl>
     <p>
      and in several other fonts:
     </p>
     <ul>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Arial" title="Arial">
        Arial
       </a>
       :
       <span style="font-family: Arial;">
        ts, dz, t, d, t, d, t, kp, b, m
       </span>
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Arial_Unicode_MS" title="Arial Unicode MS">
        Arial Unicode MS
       </a>
       :
       <span style="font-family: Arial Unicode MS;">
        ts, dz, t, d, t, d, t, kp, b, m
       </span>
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Linux_Libertine" title="Linux Libertine">
        Biolinum
       </a>
       :
       <span style="font-family: Linux Biolinum,Biolinum;">
        ts, dz, t, d, t, d, t, kp, b, m
       </span>
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Bitstream_Cyberbit" title="Bitstream Cyberbit">
        Bitstream Cyberbit
       </a>
       :
       <span style="font-family: Bitstream Cyberbit;">

     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Angle_brackets">
       Angle brackets
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      True angle brackets,
      <span class="Unicode">
       
      </span>
      , are unsupported by several common fonts. Here is how they display in your default settings:
     </p>
     <dl>
      <dd>
       ... (unformatted)
      </dd>
      <dd>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        ...
       </span>
       (default IPA font)
      </dd>
      <dd>
       <span class="Unicode">
        ...
       </span>
       (default Unicode font),
      </dd>
     </dl>
     <p>
      and in several specific fonts:
     </p>
     <ul>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Arial" title="Arial">
        Arial
       </a>
       :
       <span style="font-family: Arial;">
        ...
       </span>
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Arial_Unicode_MS" title="Arial Unicode MS">
        Arial Unicode MS
       </a>
       :
       <span style="font-family: Arial Unicode MS;">
        ...
       </span>
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Linux_Libertine" title="Linux Libertine">

       :
       <span style="font-family: Linux Biolinum,Biolinum;">
